        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1844128997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16750954927131131610">"Not yet."<br/><br/>This book, especially at the beginning and end, really hooked me. It's a book I'll be thinking about for a long time, I think. It's hard to say what I really think about this book without spoiling it, so I won't. So this review will probably be a little disjointed. Not really put together well.<br/><br/>I was in the Canadian military for a brief period over a decade ago, and - not that only a soldier would be able to empathize with this - I can easily recall that "Am I doing what I'm supposed to</span>
  <span id="freeText16750954927131131610" style="display:none">"Not yet."<br /><br />This book, especially at the beginning and end, really hooked me. It's a book I'll be thinking about for a long time, I think. It's hard to say what I really think about this book without spoiling it, so I won't. So this review will probably be a little disjointed. Not really put together well.<br /><br />I was in the Canadian military for a brief period over a decade ago, and - not that only a soldier would be able to empathize with this - I can easily recall that "Am I doing what I'm supposed to be doing?" anxiety that seems to be omnipresent post-basic training. Timothy Findley paints a perfect picture of this feeling in Robert in this book. There's a lot of focus as well on things that happened outside of the trenches that we seldom think about, which I appreciated. The normalization of violence outside the battlefield and the normalization of soldiers "going mad." Soldiers drowning, often completely alone, before they even get to fire a shot. Soldiers rewarded with harsh punishment, even death, for showing any basic decency or kindness towards the wrong sentient being.<br /><br />Powerful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16750954927131131610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13793219102654681983" style="display:none">The book is a very clever mix of a researcher trying to piece together the actions and short life of 19-year-old Robert Ross during The Great War, and the immense atrocities of the war as seen through the eyes of Robert Ross himself.<br /><br />Interesting is the plural form of the title: To me it implied both the First World War and the war Robert is fighting within himself...<br /><br />I had rated the book 4 to 4½ stars originally but the more I thought about the book and its story while writing my Dutch review for the Netherlands &amp; Flanders group's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/2010137-herfst-2014" rel="nofollow noopener">Autumn Challenge 2014</a> (message 30), the stronger my appreciation for this very cleverly written book became, which is why I ended up rating it 5 stars.</span>

  <span id="freeText1149486917802028502" style="display:none">This was a good book, but not a great book for me. It was choppy and disjointed and really lost me at times. This book is about 19 year old Robert Ross, a sensitive soul, whether it be to his treasured sister, to his fellow soldiers or to the horses he valued. <tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2045705519">
  <td colspan="2">

While historical/warfare lit is not my thing, the psychological journey and interrogation of masculinity and the hero was quite nuanced. A lot of different layers and meanings to take from this one. Surprisingly enjoyed it.</span>

<div id="review_2574228357" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2574228357" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2574228357?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32283665-the-wars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=world-war-i">world-war-i</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2574228357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10447212796334069359">For the First World War few good novels have been written, of which this book despite its quality seems to be one of the least known and popular. This I think I can understand it to some extent, the book is certainly not easy, it takes effort to appreciate it and it is characterized by a first half that is rather sluggish and most of it is not done to attract the reader's interest .<br/><br/>Of course, this change in the second half when our hero, a sensitive 19-year-old Canadian, is involved in combat op</span>
  <span id="freeText10447212796334069359" style="display:none">For the First World War few good novels have been written, of which this book despite its quality seems to be one of the least known and popular. This I think I can understand it to some extent, the book is certainly not easy, it takes effort to appreciate it and it is characterized by a first half that is rather sluggish and most of it is not done to attract the reader's interest .<br /><br />Of course, this change in the second half when our hero, a sensitive 19-year-old Canadian, is involved in combat operations in a place that is probably not the best for people with sensitivities. There, although he does not participate actively in the battle, having the role of taking care of the horses used by the army, he witnesses the horror of the First World War, the muddy fields of the battles being full of corpses, and the constant danger from bombs and gases thar is able to destroy the soldiers' psychology.<br /><br />In this second half, the author, in a very good and restrained manner, tells us the experience of our hero, as would a historian who would have at his disposal various testimonies from the people who knew him. Thus shows us the experience of war, both in the battlefields, with the soldiers fighting and many of them facing the consequences, as well as in the back where no one could remained unaffected by this brutality, especially the relatives of the soldiers .<br /><br />In other words, a book that I may not like it as much as some of the classic books on this subject bt is certainly an essential piece of work by a writer who showed the necessary sensitivity to his own depiction of the situation prevailing in the first World War. So it was definitely another interesting milestone in my journey to the literature on this important subject.<br /><br />Για τον πρώτο Παγκόσμιο Πόλεμο έχουν γραφτεί ελάχιστα καλά μυθιστορήματα, από αυτά αυτό το βιβλίο παρά την ποιότητά του φαίνεται να είναι ένα από τα λιγότερο γνωστά και δημοφιλή. Αυτό νομίζω ότι μπορώ σε ένα βαθμό να το καταλάβω, το βιβλίο σίγουρα δεν είναι εύκολο, χρειάζεται προσπάθεια για να το εκτιμήσει κάποιος και χαρακτηρίζεται από ένα πρώτο μισό που είναι μάλλον υποτονικό και στο μεγαλύτερο μέρος του δεν γίνεται κάτι για να τραβήξει το ενδιαφέρον του αναγνώστη. <br /><br />Φυσικά αυτά αλλάζουν στο δεύτερο μισό όταν ο ήρωας μας, ένας ευαίσθητος 19χρονος Καναδός, συμμετέχει στις πολεμικές επιχειρήσεις σε ένα μέρος που μάλλον δεν είναι ότι καλύτερο για ανθρώπους με ευαισθησίες. Εκεί, αν και δεν συμμετέχει ενεργά στη μάχη, έχοντας τον ρόλο να φροντίζει τα άλογα που χρησιμοποιεί ο στρατός, γίνεται μάρτυρας της φρίκης του πρώτου Παγκοσμίου Πολέμου, με τα λασπωμένα πεδία των μαχών να γεμίζουν με πτώματα και ο συνεχής κίνδυνος από τις βόμβες και τα αέρια να καταστρέφει την ψυχολογία των στρατιωτών.<br /><br />Σε αυτό το δεύτερο μισό, λοιπόν, ο συγγραφέας με έναν πολύ καλό και συγκρατημένο τρόπο μας αφηγείται την εμπειρία του ήρωα μας, όπως θα το έκανε ένας ιστορικός που θα είχε στη διάθεσή του διάφορες μαρτυρίες από τους ανθρώπους που τον γνώρισαν. Έτσι μας δείχνει την εμπειρία του πολέμου, τόσο στα πεδία των μαχών, με τους στρατιώτες που πολεμάνε και πολλοί από αυτούς αντιμετωπίζουν τις συνέπειες, όσο και στα μετόπισθεν όπου και εκεί κανείς δεν μπορούσε να μείνει ανεπηρέαστος από αυτή την βιαιότητα, ειδικά οι συγγενείς των στρατιωτών.<br /><br />Με άλλα λόγια ένα βιβλίο που μπορεί να μη μου άρεσε τόσο όσο κάποια από τα κλασικά βιβλία για αυτό το θέμα, σίγουρα, όμως, είναι ένα ουσιαστικό έργο, από έναν συγγραφέα που έδειξε την απαραίτητη ευαισθησία στη δική του απεικόνιση της κατάστασης που επικρατούσε στον πρώτο Παγκόσμιο Πόλεμο. Οπότε σίγουρα ήταν άλλος ένας ενδιαφέρον σταθμός στο ταξίδι μου στην λογοτεχνία για αυτό το σημαντικό θέμα.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10447212796334069359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3015633254" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3015633254" />
    <a title="Paul Manytravels" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44162836-paul-manytravels"><img alt="Paul Manytravels" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603803670p2/44162836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3015633254?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Manytravels" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Manytravels" href="/user/show/44162836-paul-manytravels">Paul Manytravels</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44162836-paul-manytravels?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44162836-paul-manytravels?shelf=well-above-average">well-above-average</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44162836-paul-manytravels?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3015633254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3997898483451861940">The Wars by Timothy Findley tells the story of Robert Ross, an young man from a wealthy family who serves in WW I. The book covers that entire period of Ross's life from when he first decided to join through all of his experiences in the conflict and beyond. I this, it manages to capture everything about the war experience from the level of one individual. <br/>It is not an easy read emotionally. The descriptions are accurate and graphic, and the reader must keep reminding himself that the book is fi</span>
  <span id="freeText3997898483451861940" style="display:none">The Wars by Timothy Findley tells the story of Robert Ross, an young man from a wealthy family who serves in WW I. The book covers that entire period of Ross's life from when he first decided to join through all of his experiences in the conflict and beyond. I this, it manages to capture everything about the war experience from the level of one individual. <br />It is not an easy read emotionally. The descriptions are accurate and graphic, and the reader must keep reminding himself that the book is fiction rather than history or memoir. It tells a story similar to that of All Quiet on the Western Front, detailed, graphic, engaging and horrific. <br />While other reviewers here on GR have done a great job of discussing this book and ist harrowing plot, I want to comment on the format of the book. It is a creative, innovative and perhaps unique handling of the storyline. It uses first person descriptions in some places, third person in others. It tells the story in a series of chronolocically arranged 'episodes' that somehow come together to form a coherent story. <br />Beyond the episodic descriptions of the war, the novel also uses notes from interviews conducted by a fictional writer in the book who is gathering details to write the story and also included things "found in the archives" that illustrate various aspects of the novel's plot.<br />I liked the format the author used. It made the book seem a whole lot more like a work of non-fiction rather than of fiction. It was a good story, well told.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3997898483451861940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TLpdttD/lwtfl+ptqaFeg+/5hOdBn/nuD6BrHusqcin13+bzoSD9oBvWMgqvQiwNSGC57TnnewDGFFiA+jh8iw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UmT2lIUOUqHoj0iktxqHSQ0ne90/HInHlKq1XayZiOXrAU3R9NE4CqzOkMOx+fXHqr5G10dkCyldHobDvYuGRw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/16865.Timothy_Findley">About Timothy Findley</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/16865.Timothy_Findley"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1284093571p3/16865.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/16865.Timothy_Findley">Timothy Findley

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9166607272215141195">Timothy Irving Frederick Findley was a Canadian novelist and playwright. He was also informally known by the nickname Tiff or Tiffy, an acronym of his initials.<br/><br/>One of three sons, Findley was born in Toronto, Ontario, to Allan Gilmour Findley, a stockbroker, and his wife, the former Margaret Maude Bull. His paternal grandfather was president of Massey-Harris, the farm-machinery company. He was rais</span>
  <span id="freeText9166607272215141195" style="display:none">Timothy Irving Frederick Findley was a Canadian novelist and playwright. He was also informally known by the nickname Tiff or Tiffy, an acronym of his initials.<br /><br />One of three sons, Findley was born in Toronto, Ontario, to Allan Gilmour Findley, a stockbroker, and his wife, the former Margaret Maude Bull. His paternal grandfather was president of Massey-Harris, the farm-machinery company. He was raised in the upper class Rosedale district of the city, attending boarding school at St. Andrew's College (although leaving during grade 10 for health reasons). He pursued a career in the arts, studying dance and acting, and had significant success as an actor before turning to writing. He was part of the original Stratford Festival company in the 1950s, acting alongside Alec Guinness, and appeared in the first production of Thornton Wilder's The Matchmaker at the Edinburgh Festival. He also played Peter Pupkin in Sunshine Sketches, the CBC Television adaptation of Stephen Leacock's Sunshine Sketches of a Little Town.<br /><br />Though Findley had declared his homosexuality as a teenager, he married actress/photographer Janet Reid in 1959, but the union lasted only three months and was dissolved by divorce or annulment two years later. Eventually he became the domestic partner of writer Bill Whitehead, whom he met in 1962. Findley and Whitehead also collaborated on several documentary projects in the 1970s, including the television miniseries The National Dream and Dieppe 1942.<br /><br />Through Wilder, Findley became a close friend of actress Ruth Gordon, whose work as a screenwriter and playwright inspired Findley to consider writing as well. After Findley published his first short story in the Tamarack Review, Gordon encouraged him to pursue writing more actively, and he eventually left acting in the 1960s.<br /><br />Findley's first two novels, The Last of the Crazy People (1967) and The Butterfly Plague (1969), were originally published in Britain and the United States after having been rejected by Canadian publishers. Findley's third novel, The Wars, was published to great acclaim in 1977 and went on to win the Governor General's Award for English-language fiction. It was adapted for film in 1981.<br /><br />Timothy Findley received a Governor General's Award, the Canadian Authors Association Award, an ACTRA Award, the Order of Ontario, the Ontario Trillium Award, and in 1985 he was appointed an Officer of the Order of Canada. He was a founding member and chair of the Writers' Union of Canada, and a president of the Canadian chapter of PEN International.<br /><br />His writing was typical of the Southern Ontario Gothic style — Findley, in fact, first invented its name — and was heavily influenced by Jungian psychology. Mental illness, gender and sexuality were frequent recurring themes in his work. His characters often carried dark personal secrets, and were often conflicted — sometimes to the point of psychosis — by these burdens.<br /><br />He publicly mentioned his homosexuality, passingly and perhaps for the first time, on a broadcast of the programme The Shulman File in the 1970s, taking flabbergasted host Morton Shulman completely by surprise.<br /><br />Findley and Whitehead resided at Stone Orchard, a farm near Cannington, Ontario, and in the south of France. In 1996, Findley was honoured by the French government, who declared him a Chevalier de l'Ordre des arts et des lettres.<br /><br />Findley was also the author of several dramas for television and stage. Elizabeth Rex, his most successful play, premiered at the Stratford Festival of Canada to rave reviews and won a Governor General's award. His 1993 play The Stillborn Lover was adapted by Shaftesbury Films into the television film External Affairs, which aired on CBC Television in 1999. Shadows, first performed in 2001, was his last completed work. Findley was also an active mentor to a number of young Canadian writers, including Marnie Woodrow and Elizabeth Ruth.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9166607272215141195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
